[LLM ANSWER]
 Sure, I can help you generate a questionnaire on the topic of remote working experience. Here are 10 questions that you can use:

1. How would you describe your remote working experience so far?
2. Do you feel more productive when working from home or in the office? Why?
3. What tools or technologies do you use to stay connected with your team?
4. Have you encountered any challenges while working remotely? If yes, what were they and how did you overcome them?
5. How do you maintain a work-life balance while working remotely?
6. How do you feel about the communication and collaboration with your team while working remotely?
7. How do you handle distractions and interruptions while working from home?
8. Do you feel like you have access to the same resources and support when working remotely?
9. How do you handle the lack of face-to-face interaction with colleagues and clients?
10. How do you feel about the company's remote working policy, and would you recommend it to others?

And here are the questions in a more conversational format:

1. Can you tell me a little about your remote working experience so far?
 II. Do you feel more productive working from home or in the office? And if so, why is that the case?
III. What tools or technologies do you use to stay connected with your team?
IV. Have you encountered any challenges while working remotely? If yes, what were they and how did you overcome them?
V. How do you maintain a healthy work-life balance while working remotely?
VI. How would you rate the communication and collaboration with your team while working remotely?
VII. How do you handle distractions and interruptions while working from home?
VIII. Do you feel like you have access to the same resources and support when working remotely?
IX. How do you handle the lack of face-to-face interaction with colleagues and clients?
X. And finally, what are your thoughts on the company's remote working policy, and would you recommend it to others?

Let me know if you need any further assistance!

[LLM ANSWER]
 Sure, I can help you generate a questionnaire on Onboarding with 6 questions. Here is a set of questions that could be asked:

1. How would you rate the effectiveness of the onboarding process in your company?
2. Do you think that the onboarding process is personalized enough to fit the needs of new employees?
3. Is the onboarding process long enough, or do you think it should be shorter?
4. How would you rate the level of communication between different departments during the onboarding process?
5. Do you think that the onboarding process is inclusive enough and caters to the needs of all new employees?
6. How would you rate the availability and accessibility of resources and materials during the onboarding process?

And here is the same set of questions converted into a conversation format:

* To start off, can you tell me how you would rate the effectiveness of the onboarding process in your company?
* Do you feel that the onboarding process is personalized enough to fit the needs of new employees?
* In your opinion, is the onboarding process long enough, or do you think it should be shorter?
* Can you share your thoughts on the level of communication between different departments during the onboarding process?
* Do you think that the onboarding process is inclusive enough and caters to the needs of all new employees?
* And finally, how would you rate the availability and accessibility of resources and materials during the onboarding process?

I hope this helps! Let me know if you need anything else.

1. Can you describe the feedback mechanisms that you are familiar with?
2. In your opinion, what are the benefits of having a well-structured feedback mechanism in place?
3. Have you ever encountered a situation where feedback was not collected or analyzed properly? If yes, could you please share what happened?
4. In your experience, what are the most common challenges in implementing an effective feedback mechanism?
5. How do you think technology can be used to facilitate the collection and analysis of feedback?
6. Can you share some examples of feedback mechanisms that have been particularly successful in your organization?
7. In your opinion, how can feedback mechanisms be used to improve decision-making processes?
8. What do you think is the ideal frequency of providing and receiving feedback?
9. Can you share some best practices for creating a psychologically safe environment for giving and receiving feedback?

This is a JSON object that represents a questionnaire about health and safety measures in a workplace. The questionnaire contains six questions, each with a unique code, name, type, and set of answers.

Question "Q1" asks whether the person has ever had to use the emergency exit route due to an emergency or just for fun. The answer to this question can be "Yes" or "No".

Question "Q2" asks about the importance of health and safety training for employees on a scale of 1-10. The answer to this question can be any number between 1 and 10.

Question "Q3" asks whether the person has ever noticed a situation where a colleague's negligence put their health and safety at risk. The answer to this question can be "Yes" or "No".

Question "Q4" asks about the top three health and safety measures that should be implemented in every workplace. The answer to this question can be any three items from a list of possible measures.

Question "Q5" asks whether the person has ever felt unsafe at work because of inadequate health and safety measures. The answer to this question can be "Yes" or "No".

Question "Q6" asks about the importance of regular health and safety training for employees on a scale of 1-10. The answer to this question can be any number between 1 and 10.

The questionnaire also has a unique code, name, and type. The type of this questionnaire is 3, which means it is a multiple choice questionnaire. The display order of the questions is also provided to ensure that the questions are displayed in a particular order.

This questionnaire can be used to collect data about the perception and awareness of health and safety measures in a workplace, and the data can be used to identify areas for improvement.

This JSON object contains a single questionnaire with six questions. Each question has a unique code, name, display order, and a set of possible answers. The `TYPE_ID` field is used to determine the type of question, in this case, a rating scale (1) or multiple choice (2).

  Please note that this JSON object is just a representation of the data and can be modified to fit the specific needs of the application. The structure of the JSON object is as follows:

  {
    "questions": [
      {
        "code": "CODE OF THE QUESTION",
        "name": "NAME OF THE QUESTION",
        "type": "TYPE OF THE QUESTION",
        "isRequired": true/false,
        "options": [
          {
            "text": "TEXT OF THE OPTION",
            "isSelected": true/false
          },
          {
            "text": "TEXT OF THE OPTION",
            "isSelected": true/false
          },
          ...
        ],
        "answers": [
          {
            "text": "TEXT OF THE ANSWER",
            "isSelected": true/false
          },
          {
            "text": "TEXT OF THE ANSWER",
            "isSelected": true/false
          },
          ...
        ]
      },
      ...
    ]
  }

  Each question should have a unique code, and the options and answers should also have unique codes within that question. The "isRequired" field should be set to true if the user must provide an answer to that question. The "type" field can be used to specify whether the question is a multiple choice, text, or other type of question. The "options" array is used to list the possible choices for a multiple choice question, and the "answers" array is used to store the selected options. If a question is not multiple choice, then the "options" array can be omitted.

  Here is an example of how the JSON object can be represented in JavaScript:

  let questions = [
    {
      code: "Q1",
      name: "Do you like pineapple on pizza?",
      type: "multiple choice",
      isRequired: true,
      options: [
        {
          code: "A1",
          text: "Yes, I love pineapple on pizza",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A2",
          text: "No, I don't like pineapple on pizza",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A3",
          text: "I don't have an opinion",
          isSelected: false
        }
      ]
    },
    {
      code: "Q2",
      name: "What is your favorite type of pizza?",
      type: "multiple choice",
      isRequired: true,
      options: [
        {
          code: "A1",
          text: "Cheese",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A2",
          text: "Pepperoni",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A3",
          text: "Hawaiian",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A4",
          text: "Meat lovers",
          isSelected: false
        },
        {
          code: "A5",
          text: "Veggie",
          isSelected: true
        }
      ]
    }
  ];

  This JSON object can be used to create a form with radio buttons, checkboxes, and text inputs using a JavaScript template literal and the createQuestion function from the previous answer.

  To create a form, you can use the following JavaScript code:

  let form = /*html*/ `
    <form>
      ${questions.map((question) => createQuestion(question)).join("")}
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  `;

  document.body.innerHTML = form;

  This will create a form with the questions and answers specified in the JSON object. The createQuestion function can be used to create each individual question and add it to the form.

  To create each individual question, you can use the following JavaScript code:

  function createQuestion(question) {
    let templateLiteral = "";

    if (question.isRequired) {
      templateLiteral += `<span>${question.name} <span>`;
    } else {
      templateLiteral += `<span id="question-name-${question.code}">${question.name} <span>`;
    }

    if (question.type === "multiple choice") {
      templateLiteral += "<ul>";
      question.options.forEach((option) => {
        if (option.isSelected) {
          templateLiteral += `<li id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="radio" name="question-${question.code}" id="question-option-${option.code}" checked /></li>`;
        } else {
          templateLiteral += `<li id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="radio" name="question-${question.code}" id="question-option-${option.code}" /></li>`;
        }
      });
      templateLiteral += "</ul>";
    } else if (question.type === "checkbox") {
      question.options.forEach((option) => {
        if (option.isSelected) {
          templateLiteral += `<li id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="checkbox" id="question-option-${option.code}" checked /></li>`;
        } else {
          templateLiteral += `<li id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="checkbox" id="question-option-${option.code}" /></li>`;
        }
      });
    } else {
      question.options.forEach((option) => {
        if (option.isSelected) {
          templateLiteral += `<div id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="radio" name="question-${question.code}" id="question-option-${option.code}" checked /></div>`;
        } else {
          templateLiteral += `<div id="question-option-${option.code}"><span>${option.text}</span><input type="radio" name="question-${question.code}" id="question-option-${option.code}" /></div>`;
        }
      });
    }

    return templateLiteral;
  }

  This function takes a question object and creates the corresponding HTML based on the type, isRequired, and options of the question. The name and code of the question are used to create HTML elements with unique identifiers, which can be used to select and manipulate the elements using JavaScript. The function also checks whether an option is selected and adds the "checked" attribute to the corresponding input element if it is.

  To create a form, you can use the following JavaScript code:

  let form = /*html*/ `
    <form>
      ${questions.map((question) => createQuestion(question)).join("")}
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  `;

  document.body.innerHTML = form;
